  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/368174388?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phrynne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phrynne" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne">Phrynne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8655084-phrynne?shelf=5000-books">5000-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer368174388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10175174870132366707">This is one of Robb's best books in the whole series. It really consists of two story lines, the drama of Roarke versus Eve when a woman from his past reappears on the scene, against a rather unusual set of murders and a very unlikely murderer.<br/><br/>When Eve and Roarke fall out they do it big time and the sadness is overwhelming. Now that we are in book 24 we know and love them so well that their pain is ours! I liked the way that just as things became too uncomfortable in their relationship world Rob</span>
  <span id="freeText10175174870132366707" style="display:none">This is one of Robb's best books in the whole series. It really consists of two story lines, the drama of Roarke versus Eve when a woman from his past reappears on the scene, against a rather unusual set of murders and a very unlikely murderer.<br /><br />When Eve and Roarke fall out they do it big time and the sadness is overwhelming. Now that we are in book 24 we know and love them so well that their pain is ours! I liked the way that just as things became too uncomfortable in their relationship world Robb would switch us back to the crimes and give Eve ( and us) something else to think about.<br /><br />This book requires a box of tissues and a free afternoon so you can read it in one sitting. Luckily I had both :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="10175174870132366707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3808900699192104288"><b>5 stars**</b><br/><br/>Bloody brilliant! My first 5 star for this beloved series so far. It was so good! I gotta confess that I jump one book and a novella to read this one. After reading the blurb I just couldn’t help myself! My weakness is Roarke and Eve’s relationship. I love love it when they have obstacles in their marriage. Man this one was brutal for Eve! But it’s the angst that I crave because these two are so passionate about each other. The author did such a good job handling both their emotions tho</span>
  <span id="freeText3808900699192104288" style="display:none"><b>5 stars**</b><br /><br />Bloody brilliant! My first 5 star for this beloved series so far. It was so good! I gotta confess that I jump one book and a novella to read this one. After reading the blurb I just couldn’t help myself! My weakness is Roarke and Eve’s relationship. I love love it when they have obstacles in their marriage. Man this one was brutal for Eve! But it’s the angst that I crave because these two are so passionate about each other. The author did such a good job handling both their emotions though. Yes, I wanted to shake Roarke at times when he was so clueless but, just a little. And hug Eve but she’d probably kick my butt. Lol! <br /><br /><i>”Sometimes the unspeakable can come from the decent. And sometimes, it’s possible to make yourself decent out of the unspeakable.”</i><br /><br />The case for this installment was one of the hardest I think so far, at least for me. Even though I did guess who the villain was (blame it on law and order) I enjoyed how Eve was able to piece everything together she has such a brilliant mind. It’s crazy how she gets in this set of mind of trying not to get emotionally attached to each victim but, in reality she connects to them and ends up feeling almost too much. But that’s what makes Eve so unique. Even though my OCD was killing me because I went out of order it was so worth it. Now back to the regular schedule reading lol! ❤️</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer52302487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2208221279679528293">5+ stars - Romantic Suspense/Futuristic/Mystery/Crime/Romantic Thriller<br/><br/>Wow! This is definitely one of my favorites of the series!<br/><br/>An old flame of Roarke’s shows up and causes trouble for him and Eve, and I really felt for Eve in this one. Roarke pretty much bungled things in the beginning in how he dealt, or rather didn’t deal, with Magdalena. <br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[I wanted a much stronger reaction/protest from Roarke when Magdalena called him lover and openly flirted and propositioned him, even brazenl</span></span>
  <span id="freeText2208221279679528293" style="display:none">5+ stars - Romantic Suspense/Futuristic/Mystery/Crime/Romantic Thriller<br /><br />Wow! This is definitely one of my favorites of the series!<br /><br />An old flame of Roarke’s shows up and causes trouble for him and Eve, and I really felt for Eve in this one. Roarke pretty much bungled things in the beginning in how he dealt, or rather didn’t deal, with Magdalena. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I wanted a much stronger reaction/protest from Roarke when Magdalena called him lover and openly flirted and propositioned him, even brazenly putting her hand on his thigh. He should’ve immediately and forcefully flung her hand off and told her to bugger off right then and there instead of just turning her down delicately and staying friendly. He was blind and oblivious to Magdalena’s manipulations and defensive and indifferent, which really hurt Eve. Thankfully, he finally got his bloody head out of his ass and dispensed with the conniving bitch (along with the help of Eve’s fist), and he and Eve worked things out the way they do best, with some sweaty sparring and steamy sex. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><i>“I had that hole in me, that empty space. I could have lived my life with it, content enough. I wasn’t an unhappy man.” He kept his eyes on hers as his thumb brushed lightly over the back of her hand. “Then, one day I felt something—a prickle at the back of my neck, a heat at the base of my spine. And standing at a memorial for the dead, I turned, and there you were.” He turned her hand over, interlocking fingers. “There you were, and it all shifted under my feet. You were everything I shouldn’t have, shouldn’t want or need. A cop for Jesus’ sake, with eyes that looked right into me.” He reached out, just a whisper of fingers on her face. And the quiet touch was somehow wildly passionate, desperately intimate. “A cop wearing a bad gray suit and a coat that didn’t even fit. From that moment, the hole inside me began to fill. I couldn’t stop it. I couldn’t stop what rooted there, or what grew. <br /><br />The tears came now. He watched them drip down her cheeks, wondered if she were even aware they leaked out of her. “She was part of my life. You are my life. If I have a regret, it’s that even for an instant you could think otherwise. Or that I allowed you to.”</i><br /><br />As for Eve’s murder case, it was definitely sick and twisted with some surprising plot twists. I actually had a hunch about the killer from early on. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Something about the book’s title, <i>Innocent in Death</i>, the way it was discovered that Allika’s son had died “falling” down the stairs as a toddler, and Rayleen’s behavior brought to mind the movie <i><b>The Good Son</b></i>. It definitely rang true when Eve suspected and uncovered that Rayleen was the murderer and the little sociopath’s cold-blooded nature was fully revealed. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_258719751" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/258719751" />
    <a title="Denise ~The Procrastinating Book Diva~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4133839-denise-the-procrastinating-book-diva"><img alt="Denise ~The Procrastinating Book Diva~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603068275p2/4133839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/258719751?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Denise ~The Procrastinating Book Diva~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Denise ~The Procrastinating Book Diva~" href="/user/show/4133839-denise-the-procrastinating-book-diva">Denise ~The Procrastinating Book Diva~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD   9781423316015" href="/book/show/3062797-innocent-in-death">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4133839-denise-the-procrastinating-book-diva?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer258719751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7025437446944283672">Although I'm an absolute fan of this series, I'll be the first to admit the majority of the "whodunnits" in the books are relatively easy to figure out before the halfway point. However, <i>Innocent In Death</i> was a nice change. There were so many possible suspects going in so many different directions I was never quite sure who could have killed the innocent Craig Foster. The fact that throughout the story Eve herself couldn't even pinpoint a motive only added to the mystery's mystery!! When I final</span>
  <span id="freeText7025437446944283672" style="display:none">Although I'm an absolute fan of this series, I'll be the first to admit the majority of the "whodunnits" in the books are relatively easy to figure out before the halfway point. However, <i>Innocent In Death</i> was a nice change. There were so many possible suspects going in so many different directions I was never quite sure who could have killed the innocent Craig Foster. The fact that throughout the story Eve herself couldn't even pinpoint a motive only added to the mystery's mystery!! When I finally did zero in on the killer, I dismissed her for a more "appropriate" suspect. The final showdown between Eve and the suspect was the most chilling of the series to this point. The fallout of this case is a powerful one - its rippling effects will likely continue to play out in the series because of who the killer is and the implied promise of another showdown between Eve and the killer in the distant future.<br /><br />In previous books, I've found some of the subplots placing Eve and Roarke at odds haven't always worked. At times they appear just tossed in to amp up the emotional drama between the two, but like here, when they work they are phenomenal. The re-entrance of one of Roarke's old flames caused a realistic emotional upheaval in the couple's life. It went beyond typical jealousy to the very core of their relationship. It showed both Eve and Roarke at their most vulnerable and Roberts at her most brilliant. <br /><br />This book reminded me why I love this series so much. Roberts is at her best when writing as J.D. Robb. Her ability to write multilayered, multifaceted stories filled with humor and angst is nothing short of amazing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7025437446944283672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17231005854701664636">Suspense 4.5 stars / Romance: Roarke 2 to 4 stars, Eve 3 to 5 stars<br/><br/>Excellent suspense. Despite I knew pretty early who was the murderer, the story was extremely captivating. Deep and psychologically well written. Bravo!<br/><br/>Romance. Well, I knew about this book / OW drama for a long time. I was prepared, but still pissed 😤<br/><br/>Damn, Roarke disappointed me. He was so blind and definitely led by his dick.   <span id="freeText17231005854701664636" style="display:none">Suspense 4.5 stars / Romance: Roarke 2 to 4 stars, Eve 3 to 5 stars<br><br>Excellent suspense. Despite I knew pretty early who was the murderer, the story was extremely captivating. Deep and psychologically well written. Bravo!<br><br>Romance. Well, I knew about this book / OW drama for a long time. I was prepared, but still pissed 😤<br><br>Damn, Roarke disappointed me. He was so blind and definitely led by his dick. His ex, Magdalena, whom he dated for a year 12 years ago, was a bitch, but very intelligent one. Yes, I disliked her, but I need to agree that she was a brilliant manipulater. Nothing sexual happened and if not for Roarke and Eve's unique relationship, I would even say Roarke did ok with the situation. But! This couple has its own dynamic and the situation should be judged according to it. Roarke hurt Eve. Eve showed her human side and got jealous, but not in the typical hysterical way. She was very vulnerable, but still very wise.<br><br>I wish Eve punched Roarke not only at the end, but also at the beginning and then repeatedly through the whole story. <br><br>My favorite moment - of course when she punched him and his ex. <br>It was delicious 😍😍😍<br><br>Yes! <br><br>You rock, my Eve!!!! ❤😎❤<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515574124ra/24864586.gif" width="400" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15217358084619992406">Rereading April 2018 for buddy read. Innocent is one of my Top five - probably Top three In Death books...possibly #1! :) A Five Star Read every single time!! Oh the feelings!<br/><br/>(2015 review) While the case in this book is a good one with a shocker ending, it's the character relationships that shoot this one to the top of my list of In Death books. The character relationship development is huge! When a past love of Roarke's returns to claim the love she left behind 12 years ago, Eve's world is seve</span>
  <span id="freeText15217358084619992406" style="display:none">Rereading April 2018 for buddy read. Innocent is one of my Top five - probably Top three In Death books...possibly #1! :) A Five Star Read every single time!! Oh the feelings!<br /><br />(2015 review) While the case in this book is a good one with a shocker ending, it's the character relationships that shoot this one to the top of my list of In Death books. The character relationship development is huge! When a past love of Roarke's returns to claim the love she left behind 12 years ago, Eve's world is severely rattled. Roarke appears blinded by the manipulation of his past girlfriend, &amp; Eve is devastated after witnessing a certain "look" on Roarke's face...a look usually reserved only for Eve. The heartbreak &amp; angst are high in this one as Roarke &amp; Eve struggle with out of the ordinary feelings neither are sure how to handle. Eve fears that if he could go back &amp; choose again, Roarke's choice might not be her. Roarke is upset that Eve doesn't completely trust him. The pain that they both feel just hurts my heart. Loved this book. And, oh yes, the case also has some heartbreaking scenes. This one has lots of momentous quotes. Innocent in Death is my favorite of the In Death series. A fantastic Must Read!</span>

  <span id="freeText3681354766138341630" style="display:none">First, I won't talk much on the murders on this one but the murderer? Oh man, it was damn right creepy.  So unexpected and it was like a punch in the gut.  I was thinking, can it really happen?  Is it possible?  <br /><br />Also a woman (who I want to b*tch slap)from Roarke's past is set to cause trouble and grief in their marriage.  For the first time in starting this series, I did not have hearts in my eyes while reading about Roarke.  Not happy with him here.  Men can be so dense! And also for the first time our fearless Eve feels vulnerable to the machinations of an evil b*tch.   She dubs her anti me and I don't like an insecure Eve but as a woman I totally understand her.  I hurt for Eve here.<br /><br />"Don't diminish my feelings, my instincts, or what I know.  Don't you make a joke of this or of me.  You looked at her, and for a second, the first time you saw her again, you gave her what's supposed to be mine." <br /><br />"Can you really believe this? Believe that I'd regret it was you and not her? Haven't I told you enough, shown you enough, that you're everything to me?"<br /><br />"Can you understand that that whatever it was I felt for her it's nothing.  It's so pale, so thin and weak compared to what I feel for you."<br /> <br />And when he found out at last (halleluiah) the b'tch's plan.  I loved what he said to her. <br /><br />"I'd crush you like a bug for causing my wife one single.moment of pain. Believe it. Fear it."<br /><br /> But My favorite part is the punches towards the end.  It was epic! Eve my hero!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3681354766138341630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4621203166104236074"><b>Pop quizzes were killers.</b><br/><br/>A well liked history teacher at a private school dies unexpectedly and Eve is called to investigate. The teacher was an average guy with a new wife and no enemies. Eve's investigation opens up a whole can of worms that shakes everyone.<br/><br/>Wow! Just wow! Eve not only has this case to contend with but a former lover of Roarke's shows up and causes trouble. The secondary characters of this series were pretty much in the background in this installment. There is a lot of focus on</span>
  <span id="freeText4621203166104236074" style="display:none"><b>Pop quizzes were killers.</b><br /><br />A well liked history teacher at a private school dies unexpectedly and Eve is called to investigate. The teacher was an average guy with a new wife and no enemies. Eve's investigation opens up a whole can of worms that shakes everyone.<br /><br />Wow! Just wow! Eve not only has this case to contend with but a former lover of Roarke's shows up and causes trouble. The secondary characters of this series were pretty much in the background in this installment. There is a lot of focus on Eve and Roarke. Their relationship takes a pretty big hit and the arguments are epic. I felt terrible for both of them. Poor Eve! I don't think I have ever seen her cry so much.<br /><br />The death creates many twists and turns as it leads to the killer. Lots of not so good things come out about other teachers and parents. I considered the killer briefly early on in the book but dismissed it as just a fluke. Boy was I wrong! <br /><br />This was an amazing story with some very tough subjects. I can't recommend this series enough. Every book is a true 5 star read for me. My only regret is that I waited so long to start it.<br /><br />If you are not reading this series you absolutely need to start it!<br /></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18998867-innocent-in-death">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=female-detectives">female-detectives</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=futuristic">futuristic</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2314851060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11455959105281010785"><b>Innocent in Death</b><br/>5 Stars<br/><br/>As Lieutenant Eve Dallas and her team strive to uncover the truth behind the shocking death of a well-liked teacher, another threat in the form of a former lover from her husband's past strikes closer to home and jeopardizes everything Eve and Roarke have created together. <br/><br/><b>Innocent in Death</b> is one of the best installments in the series. The mystery surrounding Craig Foster's murder is gripping and the resolution is both horrific and monstrous yet believable at the same ti</span>
  <span id="freeText11455959105281010785" style="display:none"><b>Innocent in Death</b><br />5 Stars<br /><br />As Lieutenant Eve Dallas and her team strive to uncover the truth behind the shocking death of a well-liked teacher, another threat in the form of a former lover from her husband's past strikes closer to home and jeopardizes everything Eve and Roarke have created together. <br /><br /><b>Innocent in Death</b> is one of the best installments in the series. The mystery surrounding Craig Foster's murder is gripping and the resolution is both horrific and monstrous yet believable at the same time. <br /><br />The reappearance in Roarke's life of Magdeline Percell has the potential to create an excessive amount of annoying angst. Thankfully, this is kept to a minimum as Eve and Roarke confront the issue straight on, and there is no single moment in the reader's mind that things might not turn out well. <br /><br />In sum, an excellent read, and it still amazes me that Robb finds new and incredible ways to engross her readers with this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11455959105281010785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2845205997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1759965979486072686">Lt. Eve Dallas and Detective Delia Peabody are called to the exclusive Sarah Child Academy where History teacher Craig Foster was found dead. His drink that he brought from home was laced with ricin. Dallas and Peabody begin interviewing the school's staff and the two students who found Mr. Foster. They quickly learn that some of the staff are keeping secrets. Eve finds it hard to concentrate on the case because Roarke's ex-girlfriend is back and is making trouble. <br/><br/>Another excellent mystery in t</span>
  <span id="freeText1759965979486072686" style="display:none">Lt. Eve Dallas and Detective Delia Peabody are called to the exclusive Sarah Child Academy where History teacher Craig Foster was found dead. His drink that he brought from home was laced with ricin. Dallas and Peabody begin interviewing the school's staff and the two students who found Mr. Foster. They quickly learn that some of the staff are keeping secrets. Eve finds it hard to concentrate on the case because Roarke's ex-girlfriend is back and is making trouble. <br /><br />Another excellent mystery in the Eve Dallas series. There were several suspects in this one. I kept changing my mind until I finally figured out whodunit. <br /><br />I loved the relationship portion of this story. Roarke can't see that his ex is manipulating him, and Eve is livid. I loved that Summerset was in total agreement with Eve about the whole situation. My rating: 5 Stars.</span>

<div id="review_1194762519" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1194762519" />
    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5238046-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548068787p2/5238046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1194762519?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha" href="/user/show/5238046-samantha">Samantha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6474080-innocent-in-death">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5238046-samantha?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5238046-samantha?shelf=0-kindle-book">0-kindle-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1194762519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1456491129073930366"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/74033.Innocent_in_Death__In_Death___24_' title='Innocent in Death (In Death, #24) by J.D. Robb' rel='nofollow noopener'>Innocent in Death</a> is number 24 of J.D. Robb’s “In Death” series and my introduction to the books.<br/><br/>It’s the year 2060 and lieutenant Eve Dallas has taken a case involving a young teacher’s murder. The case seems like a standard poisoning, but Eve is having trouble building a good list of possible suspects. The young teacher seemed honestly well liked in the community with no real enemies. On the home front, Eve is battling her own insecurities as an old flame from her husband’s, path has suddenly </span>
  <span id="freeText1456491129073930366" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/74033.Innocent_in_Death__In_Death___24_" title="Innocent in Death (In Death, #24) by J.D. Robb" rel="nofollow noopener">Innocent in Death</a> is number 24 of J.D. Robb’s “In Death” series and my introduction to the books.<br /><br />It’s the year 2060 and lieutenant Eve Dallas has taken a case involving a young teacher’s murder. The case seems like a standard poisoning, but Eve is having trouble building a good list of possible suspects. The young teacher seemed honestly well liked in the community with no real enemies. On the home front, Eve is battling her own insecurities as an old flame from her husband’s, path has suddenly returned.<br /><br />I devoured this book in less than 24 hours, it was pretty spectacular. I loved the futuristic and gritty world. It gave everything a great almost film noir tone to the story. The hard edge really complimented the eclectic cast of characters.<br /><br />Eve was the highlight of this for me. She’s a spectacular heroine who has a slightly skewed perspective of the world compared to everyone around her. I liked that in this installment we saw a vulnerability in Eve that offered a balance to the tough and highly competent homicide detective.<br /><br />While I loved this as an introduction to Eve Dallas and her world, I’m not sure if I would’ve enjoyed this story as much if I had already been familiar with everything. I really enjoyed how all the drama between Eve and Roarke played out. However, the main mystery lost my interest toward the end. Call me cynical, but when the villain was unveiled I couldn’t drum-up the expected horror over it. So, the drawn out ending centered around the murderer bored me.<br /><br />Despite this, I really enjoyed <i>Innocent in Death</i> and can’t wait to pick-up another book in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1456491129073930366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7832710373085612184">This series remains addictive, I can't help but jump from one to the other. Thank you to the library fairies for ensuring my reservations arrive in a steady and quick stream.<br/><br/>The book before this had me thinking I may have over-indulged in the series, and may need a break, but NOPE, I’m good to carry on, my fingers are already twitching, urging me to pick up the next one in the series. <br/><br/>This book had me so engaged, but it’s the first time ever I’ve wanted to seriously shake some sense into Roarke,</span>
  <span id="freeText7832710373085612184" style="display:none">This series remains addictive, I can't help but jump from one to the other. Thank you to the library fairies for ensuring my reservations arrive in a steady and quick stream.<br /><br />The book before this had me thinking I may have over-indulged in the series, and may need a break, but NOPE, I’m good to carry on, my fingers are already twitching, urging me to pick up the next one in the series. <br /><br />This book had me so engaged, but it’s the first time ever I’ve wanted to seriously shake some sense into Roarke, he was so obtuse at times in this, and so blinded when it came to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the she-demon Magdelana Percell or as he affectionately calls her Maggie. When he let her to call him ‘lover’ I wanted to chuck something at him, he seems to be oblivious to the connotations and that his wife won’t like it (I know I wouldn’t), and his other interactions with her - urgh. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> His behaviour and actions when it came to Magdelana, I didn’t expect from him – it was so un-Roarke like! Whilst the blinders do come off, I don’t feel like he was contrite enough!<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The punch Eve levels at Magdelana was certainly a photo moment and had me thinking yes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The murders being investigated in this one was also good and had me keen to read and read - the killer is arrogant and ice cold. <br /><br />Roarke seriously peeved me of in this book, but I did enjoy the read and see myself re-reading this.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1694616571774900727">How do you spell evil? I spell it "Raylene Straffo"!<br/><br/>I love this book for many different reasons - a horrible psychopathic child and a woman who strives to be the number one home wrecker - both of whom are extremely dangerous and also pathetic!<br/><br/>Two very good story lines with interconnecting or would that be parallel meanings/morals.<br/><br/>From the blurb: Eve Dallas doesn’t like to see innocent people murdered. And the death of history teacher Craig Foster is clearly a murder case. The lunch that his wife</span>
  <span id="freeText1694616571774900727" style="display:none">How do you spell evil? I spell it "Raylene Straffo"!<br /><br />I love this book for many different reasons - a horrible psychopathic child and a woman who strives to be the number one home wrecker - both of whom are extremely dangerous and also pathetic!<br /><br />Two very good story lines with interconnecting or would that be parallel meanings/morals.<br /><br />From the blurb: Eve Dallas doesn’t like to see innocent people murdered. And the death of history teacher Craig Foster is clearly a murder case. The lunch that his wife lovingly packed was tainted with deadly ricin. And Mr. Foster’s colleagues, shocked as they may be, have some shocking secrets of their own. It’s Eve’s job to get a feel for all the potential suspects—and find out why someone would have done this to a man who seemed so inoffensive, so pleasant...so innocent.<br /><br />Someone Eve could easily picture dead is an old flame of her billionaire husband Roarke, who has turned up in New York and manipulated herself back into his life. Consumed by her jealousy—and Roarke’s indifference to it—Eve finds it hard to focus on the Foster case. But when another man turns up dead, she’ll have to keep in mind that both innocence and guilt can be facades...<br /><br /><br />Once again we see how human our main characters are - 2 thumbs up and 5 stars!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1694616571774900727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2845424113579151243">It probably means there's something wrong with me but it was good to see a bit of a shake-up in Eve and Roarke's relationship. The introduction of Magdelena, Roarke's reaction, then Eve's reaction to his, and most of all, Summerset's, somehow...it was just all really, really good. There was some really genuine emotion going on, as usual for her books with these characters. But deeper, sadder, more difficult. For the first half of the book at least, the murder seemed almost a distraction from the</span>
  <span id="freeText2845424113579151243" style="display:none">It probably means there's something wrong with me but it was good to see a bit of a shake-up in Eve and Roarke's relationship. The introduction of Magdelena, Roarke's reaction, then Eve's reaction to his, and most of all, Summerset's, somehow...it was just all really, really good. There was some really genuine emotion going on, as usual for her books with these characters. But deeper, sadder, more difficult. For the first half of the book at least, the murder seemed almost a distraction from the main story of this woman coming into their relationship and coming between them. This was really brilliantly done, with Eve being distracted herself and possibly missing things because of it. Then it flipped, things got set right as we knew they would, and the who-done-it was really fascinating. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13213267351986979788">Yet again another compelling instalment! I both listened and read portions of this instalment and both formats had me glued to the pages. While i kind of guessed the killer early, the twists and turns of the story had me doubting my guess for a while and I really liked there way the mystery unfolded. There was also drama in the Rourke/Dallas relationship arena and I liked the way this was dealt with and the way Rourke and Eve worked through this.<br/><br/>All in all and absolutely thrilling instalment in </span>
  <span id="freeText13213267351986979788" style="display:none">Yet again another compelling instalment! I both listened and read portions of this instalment and both formats had me glued to the pages. While i kind of guessed the killer early, the twists and turns of the story had me doubting my guess for a while and I really liked there way the mystery unfolded. There was also drama in the Rourke/Dallas relationship arena and I liked the way this was dealt with and the way Rourke and Eve worked through this.<br /><br />All in all and absolutely thrilling instalment in an increasing strong strong series. can someone please hand me book 25??</span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_6665293'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665293-hot-rocks"><img alt="Hot Rocks" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1348775071l/6665293._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yNCAysAzzgtEyojlKaI+yebsNEdH2tEIjs/d3rABEqe7g29mAh5u1nHgYZEs+77iFM/73AZ/54LuXRHzzbhl7Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

"Oh, God. Oh...it's not what it looks like."<br /><br />"Bet." Eve strode in.<br /><br />Actually, Roarke thought, it was more of a swagger. He had a moment to admire it, before Eve rammed her fist in his face.<br /><br />"Fuck me." His head snapped back, and he tasted blood.<br /><br />Magdelana cried out, but even the deaf would have caught the suppressed laughter in the sound. "Roarke! Oh, my God, you're <i>bleeding</i>.
